# A basic Central Bank model

# The core model consists of 4 equations:

1. "stochastic" trend for potential output growth,  
2. Phillips-Curve relating inflation to (i) inflation expectations and (ii) lagged output gap,  
3. IS curve relating the output gap to lagged output gap and lagged interest rates.  
4. Expectations equation which is a convex combination between future and past inflation.

# The core model consists of 4 equations:

1. "stochastic" trend for potential output growth,  
2. Phillips-Curve relating inflation to (i) inflation expectations and (ii) lagged output gap,  
3. IS curve relating the output gap to lagged output gap and lagged interest rates.  
4. Expectations equation which is a convex combination between future and past inflation.

# Quick macro review..

Solow model: explaining economic growth

Production function  $\rightarrow$  Decreasing marginal returns of capital  $y = f(k)$

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/e4cba85c9376c39abd0339619a3c093439480dff95df294054f09173f0e70bea.jpg)  
Steady State

$$
\begin{array}{l} y = c + s \\ s = s f (k) = 1 \\ \end{array}
$$

Every year, part of the production is invested and part is consumed. Capital increases, but at the same time depreciates with time.

Capital accumulation or change in capital stock is given by:  $\Delta k = sf(k) - \delta k$

Why is this important?

Long-term growth is determined by  $\mathbf{k}^*$ , which importantly depends on  $\mathbf{s}$  and  $\delta$

IS-LM Model:

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/548d95bd020585fe47ba6ae84737a1b1ea3b290d360fc8d4e67a0b27ecf90a6d.jpg)

# IS-LM Model

['t'es 'el 'em 'ma-dal]

A Keynesian macroeconomic model that describes the relationship between the market for economic goods and money markets.

Alex Dos Diaz / Investopedia

I-S: Investments - Savings

L-M: Liquidity - Money Supply

- The Central Banks can control the interest rate through money market operations

# A "stochastic" trend for potential output growth

$$
\uparrow \Delta y ^ {*} = \uparrow g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

Economic growth External shock

# A Phillips-Curve relating inflation to (i) inflation expectations and (ii) lagged output gap

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/cc44686dce3835844f2809ab2c243d63352c6476cbb381f0e238b29b7e6e19c1.jpg)

# An IS curve relating the output gap to lagged output gap and lagged interest rates

$$
\downarrow y _ {t} - y _ {t} ^ {*} = \phi \cdot \left| (y _ {- 1} - y _ {- 1} ^ {*}) - \sum_ {t = 1} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \right| (i _ {- t} - E (\pi_ {- t}) - r ^ {*}) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/1a1e65b0620738c6d7b74a0478f94bfe6506d3cd315477e5d595d555710aa76d.jpg)

Output gap today

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/34f4f82bdf019308ee3671378db0665ca873f491fa3dc6060b301af86966c73f.jpg)

Lagged output gap "output gap yesterday"

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/aad06252e14e3dc54760d52bf31ec563cbb5e76f820f7f5ce56323b4ebfa0323.jpg)

"Lagged real interest rate" "interest rate yesterday"

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/b9515fd0f36fee476cda3b75636b646d7d4bafc1ff27ede16caedf28d8191d88.jpg)

External shock

An expectations equation which is a convex combination between future and past inflation.

$$
\big | E (\pi) = \big | \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + \big | (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1},
$$

where  $\pi^{ols}$  is an inflation forecast under an OLS model and  $\lambda$  is the degree of inflation stickiness,

# Three additional equations close this system:

- $r^{*} = r^{**} + \epsilon_{r}$ , where  $r^{*}$  is the "equilibrium" or "neutral" real interest rate, which fluctuates stochastically around its mean  $r^{**}$  
- $i = i^{**} + \epsilon_{i}$ , where  $i^{**}$  is the "targeted" nominal interest rate, which reflects the fact that the CB will generally be unable to achieve the desired interest rate perfectly  
- $i = r^{**} + (p - p_{-4}) + \tau_{\pi}(p - p_{-4} - \pi^{*}) + \tau_yE(gap)$ , is the CB reaction function or lor rule.

# TAYLOR RULE

Monetary policy reacts in a systematic fashion to the estimated output gap and to the deviation of annual inflation from the inflation target

$$
\boldsymbol {i} = \boldsymbol {r} ^ {* *} + (\boldsymbol {p} - \boldsymbol {p} _ {- 4}) + \tau_ {\pi} (\boldsymbol {p} - \boldsymbol {p} _ {- 4} - \boldsymbol {\pi} ^ {*}) + \tau_ {y} E (g a p),
$$

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/db57d05409f06b2d7d73a35eb81ed561a72b9bc0d368efd9c3147427d2d92cf4.jpg)

Annual inflation

Annual inflation

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/973b6bf85148f10397c6a8ea4572e9ad771d072974b31af304e17a1b159b001d.jpg)

Deviation from the target

Estimated output gap

# where

- $i$  is the targeted nominal interest rate,  
$p$  is the price level,  
- $p - p_{-4}$  is the annual inflation rate,  
- $\pi^{*}$  is the target inflation rate.

While recent inflation readings are "a cause for concern," Powell told the Kansas City Fed's annual Jackson Hole economic symposium, responding to what he sees as likely to be a temporary trend by tightening monetary policy could be a "particularly harmful" mistake.

The report "is another indication that the impulse of inflation and price pressures is still with us," Cleveland Fed President Loretta Mester told Reuters on the sidelines of a conference in New York. "It's going to take more effort on the part of the Fed to get inflation on that sustainable downward path to  $2\%$ ."

# CHOOSING A NOMINAL ANCHOR

A monetary policy framework provides a nominal anchor to the economy. What is a nominal anchor? Is a variable policymakers can use to tie down (control) the price level.

Examples: a currency peg (Argentina, Ecuador) or the money supply growth.

# A NEW ANCHOR: INFLATION

In 1990, New Zealand adopted a new approach. The NZCB started to target inflation more directly, based on its understanding of the links (or "Transmission Mechanism") from the central bank's policy instruments (interest rates) to inflation.

The inflation target prevails over any other policy objective, with the inflation forecast (predicted by models) serving as the intermediate guide.

# IT DESIGN

"Inflation targeting is a framework for monetary policy characterized by the public announcement of official quantitative targets (or target ranges) for the inflation rate over one or more time horizons, and by explicit acknowledgement that low, stable inflation is monetary policy's primary long-run goal."

Bernanke, Laubach, Mishkin and Posen (1999)

"The Governor and the Treasurer have agreed that the appropriate target for monetary policy in Australia is to achieve an inflation rate of 2–3 per cent, on average, over time. This is a rate of inflation sufficiently low that it does not materially distort economic decisions in the community."

"The inflation target is defined as a medium-term average rather than as a rate (or band of rates) that must be held at all times. This formulation allows for the inevitable uncertainties that are involved in forecasting, and lags in the effects of monetary policy on the economy."

Reserve Bank of Australia

- A major advantage of inflation targeting is that it combines elements of both 'rules' and 'discretion' in monetary policy, and is therefore often characterised as 'constrained discretion'.  
- An inflation-targeting framework combines two distinct elements: (a) a precise numerical target for inflation in the medium term and (b) a response to economic shocks in the short term.

# THREE CHARACTERISTICS OF IT REGIMES

- First, a public announcement of a target for inflation (either a point or band, symmetric on asymmetric) to be reached at a specified horizon.  
Second, an explicit (forward looking) policy decision framework to achieved the stated objective. Inflation-forecast targeting.  
- Third, a high degree of transparency and an effective communication strategy.

# THE MONETARY TRANSMISSION MECHANISM

The CB forecast the future path of inflation and compares it with the target inflation rate. The difference between the forecast and the target determines if and by how much monetary policy has to be adjusted.

That will affect long-term interest rates, then aggregate demand (and output gap) and, finally, inflation.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/091eb8ee33d85c38909b36bb9595db02dd870e61010380838108b33ca93b097a.jpg)  
Monetary Policy: Transmission and Feedback

"Inflation targeting is a policy approach based on a forward-looking assessment of inflation pressures, taking into account a wide array of instruments"

Scott Rogers (2010)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/56c5d52e70a1cb27ecbaa095c451d2675bbd8d43fc160e0d16453e5db30973a4.jpg)

# REQUIREMENTS FROM THEORY AND EXPERIENCE

? High degree of central bank independence  
? Absence of de facto exchange rate targeting  
? Transparency and accountability  
? Healthy financial system

? Goal vs instrument independence?

? What is the target horizon?

# NOT SO EASY TO IMPLEMENT

# A basic CB model

# The core model consists of 4 equations:

A "stochastic" trend for potential output growth,  

- A Phillips-Curve relating inflation to (i) inflation expectations and (ii) lagged output gap,  
- An IS curve relating the output gap to lagged output gap and lagged interest rates.  
- An expectations equation which is a convex combination between future and past inflation.

# A "stochastic" trend for potential output growth

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

# A Phillips-Curve relating inflation to (i) inflation expectations and (ii) lagged output gap

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

# An IS curve relating the output gap to lagged output gap and lagged interest rates

$$
\mathbf {y} - \boldsymbol {y} ^ {*} = \boldsymbol {\phi} \cdot \left(\boldsymbol {y} _ {- 1} - \boldsymbol {y} _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \Bigl (\boldsymbol {i} _ {- t} - E \bigl (\boldsymbol {\pi} _ {- t} \bigr) - \boldsymbol {r} ^ {*} \Bigr) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

An expectations equation which is a convex combination between future and past inflation.

$$
E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1},
$$

where  $\pi^{ols}$  is an inflation forecast under an OLS model and  $\lambda$  is the degree of inflation stickiness,

# Three additional equations close this system:

- $r^{*} = r^{**} + \epsilon_{r}$ , where  $r^{*}$  is the "equilibrium" or "neutral" real interest rate, which fluctuates stochastically around its mean  $r^{**}$  
- $i = i^{**} + \epsilon_{i}$ , where  $i^{**}$  is the "targeted" nominal interest rate, which reflects the fact that the CB will generally be unable to achieve the desired interest rate perfectly  
- $i = r^{**} + (p - p_{-4}) + \tau_{\pi}(p - p_{-4} - \pi^{*}) + \tau_yE(gap),$  is the CB reaction function or the Taylor rule.

# TAYLOR RULE

Monetary policy reacts in a systematic fashion to the estimated output gap and to the deviation of annual inflation from the inflation target

$$
i = r ^ {* *} + \left(p - p _ {- 4}\right) + \tau_ {\pi} \left(p - p _ {- 4} - \pi^ {*}\right) + \tau_ {y} E (g a p),
$$

# where

- $i$  is the targeted nominal interest rate,  
$p$  is the price level,  
- $p - p_{-4}$  is the annual inflation rate,  
- $\pi^{*}$  is the target inflation rate.

# Structure of the simulation game

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/21213043d0b99ee790bb0ba8c3ac7cccf255a677e743030a978454d4c3fec999.jpg)

# Core of the model

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/85d8d17fd6268ef9aa7d52057217c7fa19f7ad65e087d14d309aec903b0989da.jpg)  
A Basic Diagram of the Monetary Transmission Mechanism

# Performance of Inflation Targeting Regimes

Carlos G Fernández Valdovinos

Spring 2023

- Inflation targeting has become an increasingly popular monetary policy strategy.  
- There is a large literature analyzing the effect of inflation targeting in both, advanced and emerging market economies.  
- An informative (but preliminary) step is to examine inflation outcomes, inflation targets and inflation expectations over the periods during which these regimes were in place.

In all countries there have been periods where the gap between actual inflation and the target value have been fairly small…

However, the Federal Reserve states a  $2\%$  inflation target as a denominator of its monetary policy and the European Central Bank publicly aims for inflation below but close to  $2\%$ .

- While informative, the previous analysis is incomplete because they do not control for various factors that may matter.  
- Example, a reduction in the volatility of inflation expectations may reflect more stable fiscal environment.  
- What is important is to assess relative performance, and this is often done in a multi-country context where larger sizes and a control group (non IT) are available.  
- As a summary, regardless of the methodology used, most recent studies reach similar conclusions:
- The adoption of an IT regime in EM has led to lower average inflation (level and volatility) compared to a control group of non IT.  
- Adoption of IT is more effective in countries that initially lacked credibility in the management of monetary policy.

Performance improved in most countries between 1991-2000 and 2001-09, but IT economies improved more: inflation rates and average growth rates

# PRE AND POST PERFORMANCE

For the same sample, convergence to low and stable inflation after adoption of IT is striking. Non IT show improvements, but as a group the display less convergence.

Over the past 15 years, there is a stronger convergence to low and stable inflation for inflation targets than non-inflation-targeters. Growth performance is also more homogeneously better for inflation targets.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/9d4366f6d1fd3a4857f7f5a5d7a82bc4ea878ee322d44474ce3e5ec6315ba340.jpg)  
Figure 4.2. Inflation and Growth Performance<sup>1</sup> (1985-2004; percent; average on x-axis)

A more formal econometric analysis gives very similar results.

Methodology: Ball and Sheridan (2003)

IT is associated with a 4.8 pp (3.6 pp) reduction in average (standard deviation of) inflation

$$
X _ {i, t} = \phi \left[ \alpha^ {T} d _ {i, t} + \alpha^ {N} \left(1 - d _ {i, t}\right) \right] + (1 - \phi) X _ {i, t - 1},
$$

$$
X _ {i, \text {p o s t}} - X _ {i, \text {p r e}} = \phi \alpha^ {T} d _ {i} + \phi \alpha^ {N} (1 - d _ {i}) - \phi X _ {i, \text {p r e}} + e _ {i},
$$

$$
X _ {i, \text {p o s t}} - X _ {i, \text {p r e}} = a _ {0} + a _ {1} d _ {i} + b X _ {i, \text {p r e}} + e _ {i}.
$$

Table 4.3. Baseline Results  

<table><tr><td>Variables</td><td>IT Dummy Variable</td></tr><tr><td>CPI inflation</td><td>-4.820**</td></tr><tr><td>Volatility of CPI inflation</td><td>-3.638**</td></tr><tr><td>Volatility of real output growth</td><td>-0.633</td></tr><tr><td>Volatility of output gap</td><td>-0.010**</td></tr></table>

Sources: IMF, International Financial Statistics; and IMF staff calculations.  
Note: One, two, and three asterisks denote statistical significance at the 10, 5, and 1 percent level, respectively.

# Inflation Targeting The Role of the Exchange Rate

Carlos G Fernández Valdovinos

Spring 2023

# MOTIVATION

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/72186b1a185f1c996110c53d39e24b85288908a537a082df22a18e7b22a3b9df.jpg)  
Impossible Trinity

The impossible trinity states has lost relevance for EMs given that this countries have chosen an open capital account and relatively flexible exchange rates in the context of inflation-targeting regimes. But, is the exchange rate (or its volatility) irrelevant now…or not?

Better integration of EMs into the global goods and financial systems has it benefits, but brought also new challenges: large swings in capital flows (reflecting risk-on and risk-off changes in global market sentiments) and large swings in global commodity prices.

EMs monetary policy framework have increasingly focused on maintain domestic price stability. An increasing number operates an explicit inflation targeting regime, while the number using an explicit exchange rate target anchor has declined. Still, EMs inflation targets put significant weight on exchange rate considerations.

Inflation Targeting and FX Reserves  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/499c7ad5419b599bc04392f9d73fe54eee7ad42e758117e32dd92484d1dab0b8.jpg)

# IT AND FX RATE SWINGS

The evolution of capital flows have gone hand in hand with major swings in EMs exchange rates: inflows (outflows) coincided with persistent appreciations (depreciations) relative to trend. Another source of exchange rate volatility have been the dynamic of commodity prices.

There are at least two channels by which exchange rate fluctuations affect macroeconomic stability in EMs: (i) exchange rate pass-through to inflation, (ii) domestic financial conditions.

# Global financial factors

# in Inflation Targeting economies

Exchange rates and capital flows  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/1ba655a512a4e6f26d5a9e335931d24c66005919ed6e67133bab6c4a6eada527.jpg)  
EMEs = BR, CL, CO, CZ, HU, ID, IN, KR, MX, PE, PH, PL, RU, TH, TR and ZA; AEs = AU, CA, GB, NO, NZ and SE.  
1 Weighted average of bilateral US dollar exchange rates, based on GDP and PPP exchange rates; deviation from the long-term linear trend.  
An increase indicates appreciation of the domestic currencies.  
2 Sum of direct, portfolio and other investments, excluding reserves and related items.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/fb897b06de41eb752da80aa32c578867632f01458fc5aad137cb93d6e7e6c1dc.jpg)  
Emerging Markets Currencies and Commodity Prices

Impact on the CPI: (i) directly through their effect on import prices. This effect is generally larger in EMs than in advance economics due to the larger share of tradable goods, in particular food, in the consumption baskets; (ii) second-round effects, which depends on the characteristics of the domestic inflation process.

# Exchange rates have a larger impact on inflation in EMEs

In IT Economies

Exchange rate pass-through over time1,2  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/daf080fdc457a03edc97ad6d0d41a8a84234b84bf6eec7d62ad27ad59333e189.jpg)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/c2c6d76828da7da70eb67ee8a2a824f1138a33f8f10acbb029e1f04e9a361f32.jpg)  
1 Coefficients are six-year rolling window long-run multipliers from the equation Inflationit = a + b + d Inflationit-1 - ∑3j0γjΔNEERit-j + φOutputgapit + εit. Sample starts in Q1 1995. Exchange rates and inflation across countries3  
Exchange rate pass-through and inflation persistence across regions1,4  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/764ff2c19b9144a7d8d6590d83b64f185c2a0cca99866b0c1e9e8b21160d0e17.jpg)  
Exchange rate pass-through (lhs)  
Inflation persistence (rhs)

Impact on domestic financial conditions: (i) an appreciation of the domestic currency would reduce debt servicing cost and debt burden, lowering EMs borrowers credit risk, attracting even more capital and loosening financial conditions, (ii) an appreciation of the domestic currency would increase the value of local currency assets in foreign investor's home currency terms. This fact relax (risk) constraints, encouraging further investments and pushing down bond yields by compressing the credit risk premium.

# A NEW DILEMMA

Consider the following scenario of a sudden fall in commodity prices (alternatively, an increase in world interest rates) leading to:

A slowdown/ recession in economic activity

A fall in net capital inflows

A depreciation of the domestic currency

An increase in inflation.

What should the CB do?

# Typical Response of a Commodity Exporter LAC Country to a negative Shock to Terms of Trade

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/2edab487877f2ba11d4cd4e9f3e26ef5145b8c63bacd5db07905f4e1e12564a6.jpg)  
PANEL A. Inflation

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/6a54671cefa49e7609face7cc7b26e9f93081dc1f6f04fd210708a35c45af330.jpg)  
PANEL B. Net Capital Flows

PANEL C. Real GDP  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/3f65ddda3210c5327194bf591afa8dc1ce038d3b23e35b9eec68bb1d7ca4afc2.jpg)  
Note: The data correspond to Brazil 1995Q1-2017Q1. Dotted lines are 90 percent confidence intervals around SVCAR impulse responses. See Appendix

PANEL D. Nominal Exchange Rate  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/0bba0f8473bad379bc7035ba6ede7db428bd5a7cfe1c1d0d95a1ea7d4f5c4a81.jpg)  
B for details. Sowers: Authors estimations, based on Baco Central do Brasil, Bloomberg, Haver Analytics, and Ipeandata.

This new dilemma have implication for the cyclicality of monetary policy. Choosing to defend the currency/ fight inflation in recessionary times implies pursuing a procyclical monetary policy (i.e. monetary policy aggravates underlying inflation).

Country Correlations between Cyclical Components of Inflation Rate and Real GDP  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/737f6cfcdb40e23e51de47b4d07ef749fa9ea9f8f5ff721a422af107f0ea8529.jpg)  
Note: Cyclical components are calculated using the Hodrick-Prescott filter. Sources: Author's calculations, based on IFS and Haver Analytics.

Reason: in EMs, output and inflation are generally negatively correlated. As a result, unlike advanced economies, EMs have traditionally pursued procyclical monetary policy.

# Country Correlations between Cyclical Components of the Policy Rate and Real GDP

1960-2016

PANEL D. Nominal Exchange Rate

TINBERGEN RULE: states that there should be at least the same number of instruments as there are targets. Otherwise, some of the targets may not be achieved. In this context, the monetary authority can be viewed as having two targets (output and depreciation/inflation) and a single instrument.

# Constitution (Art. 285)

- "A Central Bank of the State, with character of [a] technical body is established. It has the exclusivity for currency emission, and in accordance with the objectives of the economic policy of the National Government, it participates with the other technical bodies of the State, in the formulation of the monetary, credit and exchange policies, being responsible for their execution and development, preserving monetary stability."

# Constitution (Art. 286)

- "It is prohibited to the Central Bank: 1. to grant credits, directly or indirectly, to finance the public expenses on the margin of the budget, except: I. the short-term advances of tax resources budgeted for the respective year, and II. in the case of [a] national emergency, with a substantiated resolution of the Executive Power and agreement of the Chamber of Senators."

CBP Charter (Law 489/95)

- "The fundamental goals of the Central Bank are to preserve and safeguard the stability of the currency value and promote efficiency, integrity and stability of the financial system."

CBP Charter (Law 489/95)

- "The Board members are nominated one per year, for a five year period, in order to guarantee a gradual renovation of the Board".

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/0673119b48fde1c53af2926ab06803e37c5fae01e636db70ef0f5f414f22bcfd.jpg)

Inflation under control

Stable and predictable exchange rate

Profitable and well capitalized banking sector

Good level of international reserves and trade balance surplus

# New Market Instruments

- Necessary to improve monetary transmission mechanism:  
- Liquidity facility (Overnight Deposits, Average Reserve Requirement, etc)  
- "Blind Market"  
- Electronic Payment System  
Depends on initial conditions

Credibility is crucial. Gradual tightening.

# COMUNICADO DE LA REUNION DE POLITICA MONETARIA

Asunción, 21 de Abril de 2015

En su reunion de la linea el CEOMA decidido, por unanimidad, reduir la tasa de interes de politica monetaria en 25投标人 basically  $6.25\%$  annual.

El CEOMA observa que la inflacion signaled roundo una trajectory descendente, explicada por un entorno externo que continua deflacionario y por la reversion de los recientes-Augustos puntales deprecios que se observar en ciertos productos. El Comité considera que, ante el ajuste de lasexpectativas de inflacion, es appropriado reduir la tasa de inerteras para tenermel del peril de la politica monetaria de los ultimos meses.

El CEOMA seguido mo y realizara sus intrumob ubiquean  $4,5\%$  en lo hei

MISSION: "Perspire y solar pot funecine".

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/ccf54136721351eda0a3ff6ef89ce8a957814b95f28b8a0b8617df311ef57f1d.jpg)

Asunción, 30 de abril de 2015

Acta de la Reunion de Polite Monetaria del 21/04/15 del Comité Ejecutivo de Operaciones de Mercado Abierto (CEOMA)

# Economía Internacional

En Estados Unidos, losindicadores acorteproblezmulananmoderacioninalelleducidenzimatermente2015.Siemalteiercerarespedimento delPIBpara elquarto trimeste de 2014semtuvono2.2trimestralannuallyado,seobservanemunipolitoof the actividad duranteelpremier trimeste de 2015.Aui, encuanto a laactivatumbrefuermenta,lesindencia de defusión PMI (PurchasingManagersIndex)seubicido in51enmarzo,aprobdeo 52.9de febrero. Este resultado se do por un menarminomiaslo la newordenes yuna contracción en the exportaciones.Coneste escanico,el prósimo privado de decremento del PIB para 2015yreviadoa  $3\%$  o  $2\%$  .Consenoperto almercado lateral,desempateo se mtuveno in  $5.5\%$  enmarzo,mristdasque lo ameliorado en lasnominasprivadasnoagricolasotestudé 126.000,pordebajo delverificado en fabrero(264.000).Encuanto a la inflación,el Indice de Precios al Consumidor (IPC) registró una variedad anof  $0\%$  en febrero,mristdaselaIPC nucleo se situou n  $1.7\%$ $(0.1\%)$  y  $1\%$  en me antecorneo, respectively).Aisimino,lavariabledoIndiceofPreciosofGastosofConsumopersonalPersonal ConsumptionExpensidadesIndexoPCE),medada de infiancionelevantareatheReservaFederal,se situou in  $0.3\%$  annyalthePCNucleo verificouamuito of  $1.4\%$ $(0.2\%)$  y  $1.3\%$  en enero, respectively).

En la Eurozona, la activités industrialeaugmente a su mayor niveil en die measures y la infLECTION centuna negativa. El PMI de la Eurozona se ubicoe en 52,2 en zarro, por enamice del 51,1 de febrero. This expansiion se debió principalmente a una acceleracion en el crecimiento de la produccion, un mayor impulso de las exportaciones y al aumento del employe del sector. En lineas con los resultados másfavorables de la energia, el desemploi se redujohall  $11.3\%$  en febrero  $(11.4\%)$  enenor. Por su parte, la inflacion anualocado  $-0.1\%$  en zarro, por encima del  $-0.3\%$  observado en febrero. La moderationa de la caida se debió al incrementos en losprecios observados en los secotores de servicios y aquilelres.

# Clearly explain what is the new role of the exchange rate

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/9a5adc8de3bc42385ea017d8cdad4d2477f8dbeed3e45d88a38a1c1be4609317.jpg)  
USD Exchange Rate (% Change)

# Best friend or worse enemy?

During the 80's the debate was centered on the inflationary effects of central bank financing of fiscal deficits

Coordination of macroeconomic policies helped Latin America to tame the negative effects of the last global financial crisis (Valdivia y Pérez 2013).

Coordination between monetary and fiscal policy is an ongoing topic on debates

High debt levels could affect risk perceptions generating unwanted effects following a change in the monetary policy rate (Blanchard 2004).

Combination of fiscal rules and inflation targeting regime improve fiscal performance and achieve lower inflation rates on average (Combes et. al 2014).

# Lessons from Brazil (Blanchard 2004)

Under normal circumstances, an increase in domestic real interest rates should lead to an increasing "appetite" for domestic debt and to a currency appreciation.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/8d99b2f68bbc68545d0f8fc711c5702c4f9d5c2c5ea0ee4a00f9f9b9605494c9.jpg)

However, if the interest rate increase also rise the probability of sovereign debt default, we could end-up with an opposite result.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/3943c8d5a8b80ff104b089e9e05da64f41954c4dfa2558c827ee76194a5c8a88.jpg)

The probability of having this unexpected result increases with higher debt levels, greater proportion of debt in foreign currency and elevated risk premiums.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/43e1d2c1a0bcde4464c6b875956ca6ebe5b249727757c7de2ecd9c372b958d33.jpg)

According to Blanchard (2004), this was the Brazilian case during 2002. A similar discussion was observed at end-2015.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/6d2c1374c74784bbea103a9439d8eccf9bbe6c3413b259e6791e67a2f3b8893e.jpg)

In these cases, fiscal policy, not monetary policy, is the most efficient tool to reduce inflation rates.

# FINAL REMARKS

In Paraguay, the history of nominal stability is the result of a prudent monetary policy AND a sound fiscal policy.

Implementation of an IT regime was an important step to consolidated our nominal stability record.

An unsustainable fiscal policy could destroy central bank independence, despite the institution having legal independence…."it takes two to tango"

Fiscal rules can contribute to the overall credibility of macroeconomic policies. We should not forget coordination with financial policies.

Not always all pre-conditions to adopt an IT regime will be "totally" met so……

# …Just do it!!!

# Inflation and Central Bank Independence

Carlos G Fernández Valdovinos

Spring 2023

Central banks around the globe are accomplished institutions.

While most CB conquered price stability (some earlier than others), its institutional strengths and associated credibility is frequently tested (i.e. global financial markets, pandemic).

Inflation targeting has become an increasingly popular monetary policy strategy.

Recent months have been challenging for CBs: rising inflation combined with weakened economic activity.

There is a risk of government trying to influence the dynamics of monetary policy. Example, putting more weight on GDP growth or through fiscal dominance.

All this could erode CB independence in many countries and damage monetary policy credibility for years to come.

Achieving CB independence and conquering price stability in Latin America was a rocky journey.

The index of central bank independence (CBI) is built on the spirit of the Cukierman and others (1992) index.

It considers four key elements, which lay the foundations for monetary policy formulation and implementation:

NaN. the legal mandate (policy objective)  
NaN. its governing structure (central bank governance)  
NaN. the powers to control monetary policy vis-à-vis the government (policy formulation)  
NaN. the conditions for financing government expenditure (central bank lending).

# Annex I. CBI Index—Criteria and Coding

# Central bank governor and board (0.20)

1. Term of office of the governor (0.20)

More than the presidential term 1

Same than the presidential term but the period does not coincide, or the term is not defined 0.67

Same period than presidential term 0.33

Less than the presidential term 0

2. Who appoints the governor (0.15)

Double process (executive/legislative, shareholders/executive) 1

The central bank board appoints directly or private shareholders directly 0.67

The government nominates and central bank board appoints, or vice versa 0.33

The government directly 0

3. Term of office of the rest of the board (0.15)

More than the presidential term 1

Same than the presidential term but the period does not coincide, or the term is not defined 0.67

Same period than presidential term 0.33

Less than the presidential term (for most members), or most are ex-officio members 0

4. Who appoints the rest of the board (0.15)

Double process (executive/legislative) 1

Shareholders/the legislative directly (50% or more) 0.67

The government appoints more than  $50\%$  0.33

The government directly all members 0

5. Government representation at the board (0.15)

No representation/the Minister of Finance without vote 1

The Minister of Finance has vote 0.80

Ex-officio members are minority 0.60

The minister of finance is the chairman of the board 0.40

Ex-officio members are majority 0.20

All are ex-officio members 0

6. Dismissal of Board members (majority) (0.20)

Executive proposes and legislative/independent authority confirms/approves 1 for violations codified in legislation, or office become vacant if directors stop fulfilling legal requirements for the appointment

Central bank board decides (if  $50\%$  or more of the board members are appointed independently of the government) either at its own initiative or at the request of the government for violations codified in legislation, or the law does not specify reasons for removal

Executive branch directly for violations codified in legislation 0.33

Government directly at discretion or if most board members are executive officials 0

# Central bank objective (0.15)

7. Objective/functions

Preserve price stability/financial stability/secure the working of payments system 1

Regulate the circulation of money, or preserve external value of the currency/ 0.67 promote employment, together with preserve internal value of the currency (without priority), implicit under the gold exchange standard, or only relevant functions are specified

Economic growth/development is one of the objectives (without priority) 0.33

Development is the final goal and price stability is not an objective 0

# Policy formulation (0.15)

8. Of monetary policy and policy tools (0.67)

Central bank independently, including gold-exchange standard rule and currency board arrangement

The central bank in coordination/agreement with the government 0.67

A government committee that includes the central bank sets monetary policy, or the 0.33 central bank sets monetary policy following government directions, the government approves changes in reserve requirements, or the government has veto power about monetary policy decisions

The government sets monetary policy 0

9. Of exchange rate policy (0.33)

Central bank independently 1   
The central bank, in coordination/agreement with the government. 0.67

Gold exchange standard rule/currency board

A government committee that includes the central bank, or a committee led 0.33

by the government with central bank advice, sets exchange rate policy

The government sets exchange rate policy 0

# Central bank lending (0.50)

10. Advances (0.20)

Central bank is not allowed to provide advances 1

Allowed up to  $10\%$  of government revenues, limited by monetary program, 0.75

in terms of central bank liabilities/its capital, or up to a level defined by the central bank. Can also allow limited government overdrafts

Allowed up to  $20\%$  of government revenues or bank deposits 0.5

Allowed up to  $30\%$  of government revenues or bank deposits 0.25

Allowed for more than  $30\%$  of government revenues or without limit 0

11. Other credit—securitized in the secondary market (0.15)

Not allowed except for monetary policy purposes 1

Allowed up to  $10\%$  of government revenues or bank deposits, limited by the 0.75 monetary program, in terms of central bank liabilities or its capital, or by the rules of the gold-exchange standard

Allowed up to  $20\%$  of government revenues or bank deposits 0.5

Allowed up to  $30\%$  of government revenues or bank deposits 0.25

Allowed for more than  $30\%$  of government revenues, bank deposits, or without limit; 0 the central bank transfers international reserves

12. Beneficiaries of central bank lending (0.20)

No beneficiary 1

Only the government 0.67

Plus public enterprises 0.33

Plus local governments 0

13. Interest rates charged (0.15)

At market rates 1

At rates defined by the central bank or rates cannot be lower than a floor 0.75

The interest rates cannot exceed certain ceiling, the rate is agreed with the government, or defined in the law below market rates

No explicit legal provisions 0.25

Defined by the government or the law stipulates no interest rate is charged

# Notice that:

Since the index uses information from CB's legislation, it is an index of legal central bank independence.  
The CBI index varies in a continuous scale from 0 to 1, such that the closer to 1 the higher is the independence of the CB.

The index evolution shows that independence fell shortly after CB were created and declined even more when government took control of CBs.

The trend was reversed in the 1990s with the approval of the new legislation that conferred independence to CBs.

# Fact: inflation seems to have evolved in the opposite direction of CB independence.

Figure 4: 100 years of inflation in Latin America  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/d55f8f0c5574d2f6aa6484482d0578774b2c5763f3e3ee4ba21a8dfd18fa772a.jpg)  
Sources: Argentina: Fereres (2010) and Banco Central de la Republica Argentina; Chile: Diaz and others (2010) and Central Bank of Chile; Brazil: starts in 1964, Central Bank of Brazil; Colombia: GRECO (2001) and Bank of the Republic of Colombia; Ecuador: Morillo (1996) and IMF's International Financial Statistics; Mexico: 1922 to 1940, Indice General de Precios al Mayoro de la Ciudad de Mexico, Bach y Reyna (1943) and from 1940 onward, National Institute of Statistics and Geography (INEGI); Peru: Reserve Central Bank of Peru. For other countries, IMF's International Financial Statistics, starting in 1938.

Figure 5: 100 years of central bank independence and inflation in Latin America  
(Average CBI index and  $1 +$  inflation in logs)  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/6b1320635b32453648db63bb89931584dd0668ffccb56adb91114690dc27a156.jpg)  
Source: Central bank legislation (central bank laws, reforms to the laws and relevant constitutional provisions). Inflation: IMF's International Financial Statistics and World Economic Outlook, end of year data.  
Note: The CBI index is codified based on the criteria and sub-criteria laid out in Annex 1. Inflation corresponds to the simple average in all countries each year.

Data is from a sample of 17 LAC countries for the period 1940-2019. Final data set contains between 1200 ans 1100 observations.

Using panel regressions, the baseline specification takes the following form:

$$
\pi_ {i, t} = \alpha_ {c} + \beta C B I _ {i, t} + \delta X _ {i, t - 1} + \varepsilon_ {f, i, t}
$$

The panel approach is aimed at estimating the "average" response of inflation to difference in CB independence.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/a67ed3c10ef3ec8f958a7e0a3bf6e89f4fea10a4b955d189ce1d13073888e1fe.jpg)

# A basic CB model

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

$$
\mathbf {y} - \boldsymbol {y} ^ {*} = \boldsymbol {\phi} \cdot \left(\boldsymbol {y} _ {- 1} - \boldsymbol {y} _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \Bigl (\boldsymbol {i} _ {- t} - E \bigl (\boldsymbol {\pi} _ {- t} \bigr) - \boldsymbol {r} ^ {*} \Bigr) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

$$
E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1}
$$

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

$$
\mathbf {y} - \mathbf {y} ^ {*} = \boldsymbol {\phi} \cdot \left(\mathbf {y} _ {- 1} - \mathbf {y} _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \Bigl (\mathbf {i} _ {- t} - E \bigl (\boldsymbol {\pi} _ {- t} \bigr) - \mathbf {r} ^ {*} \Bigr) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

$$
E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1}
$$

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

$$
\mathbf {y} \downarrow_ {i = 0} ^ {t} = \phi \cdot \left(y _ {- 1} - y _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \left(i _ {- t} - E \left(\pi_ {- t}\right) - r ^ {*}\right) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

$$
E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1}
$$

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

$$
\mathbf {y} \overset {\downarrow} {- y ^ {*}} = \boldsymbol {\phi} \cdot \left(y _ {- 1} - y _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \Big (i _ {- t} - E \big (\pi_ {- t} \big) - r ^ {*} \Big) + \epsilon_ {d}
$$

$$
E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1}
$$

$$
\Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y}
$$

$$
\pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} \left(y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}\right) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi}
$$

$$

\mathbf {y} - \mathbf {y} ^ {*} = \boldsymbol {\phi} \cdot \left(\mathbf {y} _ {- 1} - \mathbf {y} _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {\mathrm {i}} ^ {+} \beta_ {t} \left(i _ {- t} - E \left(\pi_ {- t}\right) - r ^ {*}\right) + \epsilon_ {d}

\begin{array}{l} \Delta y ^ {*} = g + \epsilon_ {y} \\ \pi = E (\pi) + \left[ \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \alpha_ {t} (y _ {- t} - y _ {- t} ^ {*}) \right] \cdot 4 + \epsilon_ {\pi} \\ \downarrow \\ y - y ^ {*} = \phi \cdot \left(y _ {- 1} - y _ {- 1} ^ {*}\right) - \sum_ {t = 0} ^ {4} \beta_ {t} \binom {\downarrow} {i _ {- t}} - 1 \\ E (\pi) = \lambda \pi^ {o l s} + (1 - \lambda) \pi_ {- 1} \end{array}
$$

# Fiscal budget restrictions at work: explaining decades of instabilities

Carlos G Fernández Valdovinos

Spring 2022

# Motivation

# The lack of fiscal discipline has been at the root of most of LAC's macroeconomic instability (and poor GDP relative performance)

Real GDP per capita relative to the US  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7f7579109755a4e53fe3fd0296b708a2353b782d06ef8984a6c7108e3b6ac469.jpg)  
Source: Maddison Project (2020).

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/b5d1f111d95bcb55a7716ffc5a37c79ed8c5a4058ed0136176e52e4f31047521.jpg)  
Real GDP per capita relative to the US

Fact 1: coincidental with periods of poor economic performance countries in Latin America experienced several economic crisis.  
Fact 2: specific symptoms varied: high inflation rates, balance of payment crisis and large devaluations, banking crisis, defaults on debt, etc.  

- Hypothesis: all economic crisis in Latin America have been the result of poorly designed or poorly implemented macro-fiscal policies.

# LAC HISTORY OF MACRO INSTABILITY

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/c769172565a7e8b8905b0ba6cfadc56ee0969fa9067878d879dc1070f3968d56.jpg)

TASK: we develop a conceptual framework, which focuses on the relationship between the joint determination of fiscal and monetary policies and their interaction with nominal instability.

The Monetary and Fiscal History of Latin America Project was launched in 2013 by the University of Chicago's Becker Friedman Institute.

# Conceptual framework

The framework, developed by Sargent (1986), consist of two main ideas (blocks):

A budget identity for the consolidate government  
A demand for real money.

The first block is the government budget identity. Government is constraint on its decisions, can choose only three of the following four policies:

Total Expenses  
Total Revenues  
Increases in Debt  
Increases Money supply

# Main idea

Government has two ways of financing its (exogenous) deficit:

Issuing debt  

- Printing money

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7415f3e6d4c6d66587c8a1478a94d9f7e7d202225ee741526b1c356f923e1c36.jpg)  
Budget identity

- The second block is a demand for real money balances. The demand for real money equation establishes a relationship between the general price level, short-term interest rate, total real income and some measure of money.

# Demand for real money balances equation:

$$
\frac {M _ {t}}{P _ {t}} = \gamma - \delta \left(\frac {P _ {t + 1}}{P _ {t}}\right)
$$

where  $M_{t}$  is the outstanding stock of money,  $P_{t}$  is the price level, and  $\gamma > \delta$ . Solving for the difference equation above, we get*:

$$
P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \sum_ {j = 0} ^ {\infty} \left(\frac {\delta}{\gamma}\right) ^ {j} M _ {t + j}
$$

# Main result

Sustained increases in money growth generate sustained increases in prices.

# CONCEPTUAL FRAMEWORK

If we let:

- $\xi_{t} = \left(\frac{E_{t}P^{*}}{P_{t}}\right)\longrightarrow$  real exchange rate  
- $\theta_{t}^{N} = \frac{B_{t}}{P_{t}y_{t}}; \theta_{t}^{r} = \frac{b_{t}}{y_{t}}; \theta_{t}^{*} = \frac{B_{t}^{*} / P_{t}^{*}}{y_{t}}; m_{t} = \frac{M_{t}}{P_{t}Y_{t}}; d_{t} = \frac{P_{t}D_{t}}{P_{t}y_{t}}; \tau_{t} = \frac{P_{t}T_{t}}{P_{t}y_{t}}$  
- $g_{t} = \frac{y_{t}}{y_{t - 1}};\pi_{t} = \frac{P_{t}}{P_{t - 1}};\pi_{t}^{*} = \frac{P_{t}^{*}}{P_{t - 1}^{*}}\longrightarrow$  growth rates

variables aspercent ofGDP

We can write the budget constraint (as percentage of GDP) as:

$$
\begin{array}{l} (\theta_ {t} ^ {N} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N}) + (\theta_ {t} ^ {r} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r}) + (\xi_ {t} \theta_ {t} ^ {*} - \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*}) + (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \bigg (1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} \bigg) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t} \\ \end{array}
$$

# CONCEPTUAL FRAMEWORK

We can write the budget constraint as:

$$
\begin{array}{l} (\theta_ {t} ^ {N} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N}) + (\theta_ {t} ^ {r} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r}) + (\xi_ {t} \theta_ {t} ^ {*} - \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*}) + (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \left(1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}}\right) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t} \\ \end{array}
$$

- LHS: the first three terms represent increases in debt-to-output ratios in the three different types of debt: nominal, indexed, and foreign currency.  
- LHS: the fourth term represents increases in high-powered money (as percentage of GDP) and the last one measures seigniorage.  
- RHS: the first three terms represent the service costs on each of the three debt types (discounted by GDP growth).  
- RHS: the final two terms represent the fiscal deficit, including the extraordinary transfers  $T_{t}$ , as a fraction of output.

# CONCEPTUAL FRAMEWORK

We can write the budget constraint as:

$$
\begin{array}{l} (\theta_ {t} ^ {N} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N}) + (\theta_ {t} ^ {r} - \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r}) + (\xi_ {t} \theta_ {t} ^ {*} - \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*}) + (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \left(1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}}\right) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t} \\ \end{array}
$$

- LHS: the first three terms represent increases in debt-to-output ratios in the three different types of debt: nominal, indexed, and foreign currency.  
- LHS: the fourth term represents increases in high-powered money (as percentage of GDP) and the last one measures seigniorage.  
- RHS: the first three terms represent the service costs on each of the three debt types (discounted by GDP growth).  
- RHS: the final two terms represent the fiscal deficit, including the extraordinary transfers  $T_{t}$ , as a fraction of output.
- Result: sustained fiscal deficits do not necessarily imply that inflation needs to increase as there is the possibility of issuing bonds.  
- Still, the government may eventually face constraints in its ability to borrow.  
- As a first approximation, the limit should be related to the ability of the government to generate future surpluses:

$$
\theta_ {t} ^ {N} + \theta_ {t} ^ {r} + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t} ^ {*} \leq \Theta
$$

where,  $\Theta$  is an exogenously specified number.

Debt financing does not eliminate the interdependence between fiscal and monetary policy, it only postpone the debate. Once the debt is high enough, two possible outcomes:

- Fiscal dominance = when fiscal authority wins and the central bank monetizes deficits (e.g. LAC).  
- Monetary dominance = when monetary authority wins and the fiscal authority generates surpluses (e.g. US in the 90s).

Fiscal budget constraint when the debt limit is binding and the financing needs are still positive:

$$
\begin{array}{l} (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \left(1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}}\right) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t}, \\ \end{array}
$$

Inflation is unavoidable!

# ARGENTINA

# It is always and everywhere a monetary phenomenon

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7421aeab8b3d2b8b305648d3ab923bae55af9365a7c7271a8189adf2a17ae5c0.jpg)  
Fiscal Deficit and CB transfers to Treasury  
Data acumulados en el 2021

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/b21076af0cce305406daa02cace05196b615fa88180a511cd972a2050aaf0eb8.jpg)  
Annual Inflation In percentage

- With minor modification, it is possible to accommodate balance of payments crises when countries chose to fix devaluation rates. Krugman (1979)  
Assuming PPP holds:

$$
P _ {t} = E _ {t} P _ {t} ^ {*}
$$

- Then, given foreign inflation and a fixed exchange rate, the government pins down domestic inflation rate.  
- Under this conditions, the real money demand equation determines the path for the money supply (impossible Trinity).

$$
\frac {M _ {t}}{P _ {t}} = \gamma - \delta \left(\frac {P _ {t + 1}}{P _ {t}}\right)
$$

- Fiscal budget constraint for a country which has reached its debt limit and has a fixed exchange rate regime.

$$
\begin{array}{l} (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \left(1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}}\right) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t}, \\ \end{array}
$$

- Step 1: despite the fiscal deficit, the exchange rate regime contain domestic inflation at the cost of a systemic decline in the stock of reserves.  
- Step 2: a balance-of-payments crisis unfolds after a sequence of positive deficits that are "financed" with those reserves.
- Under a speculative attack the central bank would not have enough reserves to support the exchange-rate regime  $\rightarrow$  devaluation ensues, which, through the PPP constraint, pushes domestic prices upward.  
- Thus, exchange rates regimes may delay the inflationary consequences of chronic deficits. This delay is paid for by the reduction in the stock of foreign reserves held at the central bank.

# The Case of Argentina

# ARGENTINA: A STORY OF MAJOR MACRO INSTABILITIES

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/f141869a1ec4f0ad1621300f9c87f6039ba9057cf13f6ce06b4fb8496276f123.jpg)

- Several symptoms: several balance of payment crises, three periods of hyperinflation, two defaults on government debt, three banking crises.  
- A number of monetary reforms: 13 (thirteen) zeros removed from currency!  
- But only one root: inability to tame fiscal deficits.  
Four sub-periods:

1960-1977: economy closed to capital movements, high growth.  
1977-1990: first liberalization of financial markets and increase in foreign debt, default, money printing, hyperinflation.  
1991-2001: currency board, second liberalization of financial markets and successful debt renegotiation, low inflation, high growth.  
2002-2017: end of currency board, default, country excluded from international financial markets, efforts to renegotiate debt, moderate growth, high inflation but moderate relative to the past.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/80e37d185f7da45f179f138093082a28ec00e9375370e39a137fade344911f2a.jpg)  
Log of per capita GDP

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/5d0db3ca5e7f622cfbd31c68b5d0182925a65ebaf5244ac277f599285d073d45.jpg)  
Annual inflation rate (log scale)

# ARGENTINA: A STORY OF MAJOR MACRO INSTABILITIES

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/4ff8c6fd02e7d6cbb437f70854bfbdff99a4a25d00af1a157a403d7f2e2f0687.jpg)  
Simulated public national debt fixing the RER (Percent of GDP)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7b34b75b46af8a38cc04239df40c6c1ce8952a126dec2ce4abadea7afcd4879e.jpg)  
Total Public Debt (Percent of GDP)

- On the budget accounting exercise, the table uses independent measures for all components of the budget constraint (i.e. do not match exactly).  
- Off-the-book expenditures (transfers): 2002 banking crisis resolution.  
1960-1975: sizeable primary deficits, small interest payments given low debt levels, monetary financing, high inflation rates, negative transfers.  
1976-1990: high primary deficits, bigger interest payments, large increases in government debt, seigniorage and inflation substantially higher.  
1991-2001: radical change in behavior, negligible seigniorage due to currency board, positive transfers given bond issuance to pay pension holders.  
- 2002-2017: resurgence in seigniorage, primary deficit negative (but that changed in final years), large transfers due to off-budget expenses after the 2002 banking crisis.

# The Case of Brazil

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/f70686b561dad8472ea3a91fac0305ab449085d851965129d8a2636be9e38e19.jpg)

Inflation and stabilization plans  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/31e5ab160843e76b1c4736889deda1be22ca68098a027c58033fc13e92e90784.jpg)  
Source: Ayres, Garcia, Guillen and Kehoe, 2019.

- Brazil's economic history between 1960 and 2016 is a history of economic stabilization plans.  
- The first one (PAEG or Government Economic Action Plan) in 1964 looked to stabilized inflation of around 100 percent per year.  
- The last one (Real) in 1994 looked to stabilized inflation of around 90 percent per MONTH.  
- Three sub-periods:

1960-1980: fast economic growth, high inflation and moderate deficits.  
1981-1994: slow growth with hyperinflation, high deficits severe balance of payment crisis.  
1995-2016: moderate growth with low inflation and low deficits.

- The high-inflation period (1960-1994) was characterized by a combination of fiscal deficits, passive monetary policy, and constraints on debt financing.  
- The transition to the low-inflation period (1995-2016) was characterized by improvements in all of these features.  
- Two singular characteristics: (i) a long period of very high inflation, over 100 percent (1980-1994); (ii) modest levels of deficits for very high underlying inflation rates.  
- Two features of the economy: (ii) a poor institutional framework in which other public entities besides the monetary authority had indirect control over money issuance; (ii) a high degree of indexation in the economy to past inflation with a passive monetary policy.  
- Together, these features created the time inflation inertia and gave many the illusion that rising prices could be cured without major improvements in the fiscal stance.

# BRAZIL: A STORY OF STUBBORN INFLATION

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/d6d5a9c820c40b69f2cf19335c4ac65cf4ac3b447f4c0d77e93c6ca1ec117b0e.jpg)  
Real GDP per capita

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/c17e79fcc3b6a2b595497fcaf336718cccdbea435c30b669a2259e03bcf74d4c.jpg)  
Annual inflation rate (log scale)

Deficit  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/3aa460ba6bc1fd934b35638bf376218b8c065d925a4945cabbd774b83bb00cca.jpg)  
Source: Ayres, Garcia, Guillen and Kehoe, 2019.

1960-1964: markets for government debt securities were underdeveloped, thus there were restrictions on domestic and external debt financing. Primary deficits had to be financed with seigniorage revenues.  
1964-1972: after the PAEG stabilization plan, deficits were reduced and the government were able to issue domestic debt securities.  
1973-1980: rising debt financing in external markets and seigniorage revenues, associated with higher interest payments and rising transfers (SOEs investments).  

- 1981-1994: debt crisis, so seigniorage revenues finance the payments of (principal and interest) the external debt as well as the primary deficits.  
1995-2002: improvements in fiscal deficits lower seigniorage.  
2003-2011: replacement of external debt by domestic debt.  
2012-2016: deterioration in fiscal balance financed by domestic debt.

Notes: See appendix C for a description of the budget constraint. Transfers are computed as  
$(8) = (1) + (2) + (3) + (4) - (5) - (6) - (7).$

# The Case of Paraguay

# PARAGUAY: A TYPICAL BOP CRISIS

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/39c108653e093283d90792c11ea64d21092656b3bfcd86f56aea6fc8db2ad54f.jpg)

- Best macroeconomic performance in the region.  
- Nevertheless, still one of the poorest countries in LAC.  
- Paraguay has narrowed income gap, but efforts were not sufficient.  
- Low levels of income per capita, low-quality infrastructure and education.  
- Macroeconomic stability is necessary but not sufficient.

In the period of analysis, we can observe:

- Political will to keep inflation low.  
- Some hicups in the process.  
- Three monetary regimes:
- Between 1960 and 1980, there was a fixed exchange rate regime.  
- Between 1981 and 1990, the central bank financed government deficits.  
- After 1992, an independent central bank conducted monetary policy to keep inflation low.

Real GDP per capita*  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/5331eb28dc95ddf141ba1f4f23c928b74e1868851c2f0e79fdadd1be49e0dcaa.jpg)  
*Log (base 2) of real GDP per capita and 2 percent growth trend.

Assuming PPP holds:

$$
P _ {t} = E _ {t} P _ {t} ^ {*}
$$

- Then, given foreign inflation and a fixed exchange rate, the government pins down domestic inflation rate. Under this conditions, the real money demand equation determines the path for the money supply.  
In a country with debt constraints and fixed exchange rate regime.

$$
\begin{array}{l} (m _ {t} - m _ {t - 1}) + m _ {t - 1} \left(1 - \frac {1}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}}\right) \\ = \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {N} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t}} - 1\right) + \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {r} \left(\frac {r _ {t - 1}}{g _ {t}} - 1\right) + \xi_ {t} \theta_ {t - 1} ^ {*} \left(\frac {R _ {t - 1} ^ {*}}{g _ {t} \pi_ {t} ^ {*}} - 1\right) + d _ {t} + \tau_ {t}, \\ \end{array}
$$

- It is not possible to print money. Given a value for the primary deficit and the interest payments, the only way to satisfy the budget identity its through adjustments in transfers,  $\tau_{t}$ .  
- This terms reflects adjustments on Central Banks' reserves.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/75610eaa54ce34a5047988c690395c21f9eb777dc10c1b6f059c717d6e0253a2.jpg)  
Deficit (Percent of GDP)

# Appendix

# Demand for real money balances equation solution (step-by-step)

We start with:

$$
\frac {M _ {t}}{P _ {t}} = \gamma - \delta \left(\frac {P _ {t + 1}}{P _ {t}}\right)
$$

Solving for  $P_{t}$  returns:

$$
P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} (M _ {t} + \delta P _ {t + 1})
$$

Replacing  $P_{t + 1}$  we get:

$$
\begin{array}{l} P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \bigg (M _ {t} + \delta \left(\frac {1}{\gamma} (M _ {t + 1} + \delta P _ {t + 2})\right) \bigg) \\ P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \left(M _ {t} + \frac {\delta}{\gamma} M _ {t + 1} + \frac {\delta^ {2}}{\gamma} P _ {t + 2}\right) \\ \end{array}
$$

Replacing  $P_{t + 2}$  we get:

$$
\begin{array}{l} P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \bigg (M _ {t} + \frac {\delta}{\gamma} M _ {t + 1} + \frac {\delta^ {2}}{\gamma} \bigg (\frac {1}{\gamma} (M _ {t + 2} + \delta P _ {t + 3}) \bigg) \bigg) \\ P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \left(M _ {t} + \frac {\delta}{\gamma} M _ {t + 1} + \frac {\delta^ {2}}{\gamma^ {2}} M _ {t + 2} + \frac {\delta^ {3}}{\gamma^ {2}} P _ {t + 3}\right) \\ \end{array}
$$

If we continue replacing  $P_{t + 3}, P_{t + 4}, P_{t + 5}, \ldots$ :

$$
P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \bigg (M _ {t} + \frac {\delta}{\gamma} M _ {t + 1} + \frac {\delta^ {2}}{\gamma^ {2}} M _ {t + 2} + \frac {\delta^ {3}}{\gamma^ {3}} M _ {t + 3} + \frac {\delta^ {4}}{\gamma^ {4}} M _ {t + 4} + \frac {\delta^ {5}}{\gamma^ {5}} M _ {t + 5} + \dots \bigg)
$$

Which is exactly what our solution states:

$$
P _ {t} = \frac {1}{\gamma} \sum_ {j = 0} ^ {\infty} \left(\frac {\delta}{\gamma}\right) ^ {j} M _ {t + j}
$$

# FISCAL CONSOLIDATIONS DO HAVE "HEAVY" POLITICAL COSTS

# Design matters

How tax reforms are designed and implemented affects whether political incumbents are reelected.

(percent)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/268d6843268d2e90f490dcdf594097a7cb6a7136885710a4a03f52a7f7dee90b.jpg)

Source: Chen and others (2019).

Note: Selected results, with a significant test for the difference in regression coefficients (beta). For instance, baseline (first column) results indicate that a 1 percent of GDP tax consolidation reform lowers the probability of government party reelection by 8 percent. CIT and PIT refer to corporate income tax and personal income tax, respectively. * = Reforms motivated by other factors are not reported.

Variables are deflated by the GDP deflator. The bias is defined by the absolute variation of capital spending share between 2016 and 1980.

Sources: LCRCE, based on data from WEO and National Accounts.

Correlation cyclical component of tax indexes and real GDP  
![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7686df291202e291fb70606bb3abea51922bc665c41707e3b8d9422bbf3f7932.jpg)  
Notes: Cyclical components are calculated using the Hodrick-Prescott filter with the standard smoothing parameter for annual data (6.25). Tan, red and blue bars denote non-LAC developing, LAC, and industrial countries respectively. *, **, and *** indicate significance at the 10, 5, and 1 percent level of a standard two-tailed means test respectively. † indicates significance at 10.1% level. Sources: Vegb and Vuletin (2015).

Estimate the following equation:

$$
\Delta \frac {B}{Y} = \beta_ {0} + \beta_ {1} \left(\frac {Y - Y ^ {*}}{Y ^ {*}}\right) + \beta_ {2} \left(\frac {B}{Y _ {t - 1}}\right) + \gamma^ {\prime} x + f _ {i} + \varepsilon
$$

where,  $B$  is fiscal balance,  $Y$  is nominal GDP,  $Y^{*}$  is potential GDP,  $x$  is a vector of other control variables,  $f_{i}$  is a country fixed effect and  $\varepsilon$  is an error term.

# Econometric results

Dependent variable:  $\Delta$  Adjusted primary fiscal balance

Cyclical components are calculated using the Hodrick-Prescott filter with the standard smoothing parameter for annual data (6.25). *, **, and *** indicate significance at the 10, 5, and 1 percent level for the regression slope respectively. Sources: Fitch and LCRCE, based on data from WEO and National Accounts.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/4c6ac2e9ac1d841bd851feb31a8d14482aff34357082cba02c410d2f3ecf780e.jpg)

# FISCAL ADJUSTMENT: REDUCING OUTPUT LOSSES

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/0c6c6466d5ec9195f760634d35bfdf31f291bfd51b2b29f77ce4dee2f95efdb7.jpg)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/8c4b5b78a3f409d17625f85fd3aa8b0c9df386fd507f72da743103af6343b4c4.jpg)  
Government Gross Debt (% of GDP)

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/7e20f3146b3a01caa7456bccee2aadb537f180b656bf102b04c160e2c0425a60.jpg)

- Equation to estimate the average impulse response of output to fiscal consolidation using panel data analysis:

$$
g _ {i t} = \alpha + \sum_ {j = 1} ^ {2} \beta_ {j} g _ {i, t - j} + \sum_ {s = 0} ^ {2} \beta_ {s} A B F C _ {i, t - s} + \mu_ {i} + \lambda_ {t} + v _ {i t},
$$

The equation has the growth rate of real GDP  $(\mathrm{g})$  as the dependent variable. The explanatory variables are the current and lagged values of the fiscal consolidation measures, where ABFC is the estimated size of the action-based fiscal consolidation measures as a percent of GDP.

# FISCAL ADJUSTMENT: REDUCING OUTPUT LOSSES

# Impact of fiscal consolidation on GDP and Unemployment

Fiscal consolidation is normally contractionary. A fiscal consolidation equal to 1 percent of GDP typically reduces real GDP by about 0.5 percent and raises the unemployment rate by about 0.3 percentage point.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/bd720c244fd63d39bc2515ca7ade5e6d7a0078b0cb7f284938023f97f9fdaf26.jpg)  
Source: IMF staff calculations. Note:  $t = 1$  denotes the year of consolidation. Dotted lines equal one standard error bands.

# FISCAL ADJUSTMENT: REDUCING OUTPUT LOSSES

# Response of monetary conditions to fiscal consolidation

Interest rate cuts and a decline in the value of the domestic currency usually play a key supportive role during episodes of fiscal consolidation.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/3718d91c5ff913af392804b9700fadddd86b6b7d5d771414e26ef97a6b28b8f7.jpg)  
Source: IMF staff calculations. Note:  $t = 1$  denotes the year of consolidation. Dotted lines equal one standard error bands.

# Response of GDP components to fiscal consolidation

Net exports typically expand in response to fiscal consolidation, providing a key cushion for GDP. In contrast, domestic demand contracts. The boom in net exports reflects both an increase in exports in response to the real exchange rate depreciation and a decline in imports reflecting the fall in income.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/e53b0900d01affe3ac4b2af0135d1fe3f5bbc22c0ca5ecd44b8cc1440e91d1e9.jpg)  
Note:  $t = 1$  denotes the year of consolidation. Dotted lines equal one standard error bands.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/f0cbf2fc3ac995990f2b8e7e7cf3b3928271fa8143a94901ae95d70ff9f042c0.jpg)  
Source: IMF staff calculations.

# Impact of fiscal consolidation and monetary conditions Impact of a  $1\%$  GDP Fiscal Consolidation

Why are spending-based consolidations less contractionary? Partly because they benefit from monetary stimulus, whereas tax-based adjustments feature monetary tightening.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/ce158f561aff9399a24ffa1b8a0023917b5da17aacac92fcf610dbc0353be2ab.jpg)

# Impact of fiscal consolidation on output, by level of risks Impact of a  $1\%$  GDP Fiscal Consolidation

Fiscal consolidation preceded by high perceived sovereign risk is less contractionary than when preceded by low perceived default risk. But even for the group with high perceived risk, fiscal retrenchment rarely triggers faster growth. Exceptions include Denmark (1983) and Ireland (1987)—two cases of fiscal consolidation studied by Giavazzi and Pagano (1990)—which were expansionary.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/43d9d175c5e5bafd5e553570fd9db428edcb5a9f4eb8617055439729c9197563.jpg)  
Source: IMF staff calculations.  
Note:  $t = 1$  denotes the year of consolidation. Dotted lines equal one standard error bands.

# RULES VS DISCRETION? VIRTUE IS IN THE MIDDLE

# Operational Rules

# Fiscal rules should be able to correct policy biases (sustainability and procyclicality) and perform he task efficiently (simplicity, resilience, ease of monitoring, etc.)

# FISCAL FUNCTIONS

- Smoothing the economic cycle.  
- Fostering long-term growth.  
- Promoting inclusiveness.

# DESIRED FEATURES

Sustainability  
Stabilization  

- Simplicity  
- Operational guidance  
- Resilience  
- Easy of monitoring and enforcement

# GOOD FISCAL FRAMEWORK

One fiscal anchor linked to final objective (Debt/GDP)  
One or more operational rules on fiscal

Note: Debt rules set an explicit limit or target for public debt as a percent of GDP. Budget balance rules (structural and nonstructural) constrain the variable that primarily influences the debt ratio and are largely under the control of policymakers. Revenue rules set ceilings or floors on revenues and are aimed at boosting revenue collection and/or preventing an excessive tax burden. Expenditure rules set limits on total, primary, or current spending. Fiscal rules, data come from the "IMF Fiscal Rules Dataset, 2016" and Schaechter et al. (2012).

# Assessment of fiscal rules

<table><tr><td colspan="2">Budget Balance Rules</td></tr><tr><td>Overall Balance</td><td>Golden</td></tr><tr><td>+ Easy to communicate/monitor</td><td>+ Protect public investment</td></tr><tr><td>+ Clear operational guidance</td><td>+ Intergenerational equity</td></tr><tr><td>- Can lead to procyclicality</td><td>- Weak link to debt sustainability</td></tr><tr><td>- Could lead to changes in composition</td><td>- Creative Accounting</td></tr><tr><td>Cyclically Adjusted and Structural</td><td>Over the Cycle</td></tr><tr><td>+ Foster economic stabilization</td><td>+ Good stabilization properties</td></tr><tr><td>+ Good operational guidance</td><td>- May entail too loose/tight stance</td></tr><tr><td>- Difficult to compute and monitor</td><td>- Difficult to monitor and enforce</td></tr><tr><td>Expenditure Rules</td><td>Revenue Rules</td></tr><tr><td>+ Easy to communicate/monitor</td><td>+ Raise revenues or limit tax burden</td></tr><tr><td>+ Allow macroeconomic stabilization</td><td>- No direct link to debt sustainability</td></tr><tr><td>+ Clear operational guidance</td><td>- Can lead to procyclicality</td></tr><tr><td>+ Can ensure debt sustainability if well designed</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>- Could lead to changes in composition</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>- May reduce incentive to mobilize revenues</td><td></td></tr></table>

Source: IMF staff

"Impose limits (ceiling) on the headline fiscal balance (deficit), sometimes with the exclusion of some expenditures or revenue items"

- Positive: simple and they are good for debt sustainability goals.  
- Negative: can lead to procyclical policy and bias against investment.

# DERIVATION OF CYCLICALLY ADJUSTED FISCAL BALANCE

Cyclically Adjusted Balance (CAB) = Cyclically adjusted revenue  $(\mathbf{T}^{\mathrm{CA}})$  - Cyclically adjusted expenditure  $(G^{\mathrm{CA}})$

$$
T ^ {C A} = T \left(\frac {Y ^ {P}}{Y}\right) ^ {\varepsilon_ {T, Y}}
$$

T: Actual Revenue

Y: Output

$Y^{P}$ : Potential Output

$\varepsilon_{T,Y}$ : Revenue elasticity

$$
G ^ {C A} = G \left(\frac {Y ^ {P}}{Y}\right) ^ {\varepsilon_ {G, Y}}
$$

G: Actual Expenditure

Y: Output

$Y^{P}$ : Potential Output

$\varepsilon_{G,Y}$ : Expenditure elasticity

If elasticity is positive: revenue is procyclical

If elasticity is negative: expenditure is countercyclical

- Elasticity measures how much revenues or expenditures increase (\%) when output increases in  $1\%$  
- It is necessary to have a good approximation of potential output, otherwise there can be several errors.

# DERIVATION OF CYCLICALLY ADJUSTED FISCAL BALANCE

# CALCULATING ELASTICITY

There are several econometric/statistic methods to calculate elasticity. However, the following values are commonly used in economic literature:

- Revenue Elasticity = 1 (or greater)  
- This means that a  $1\%$  output increase implies a  $1\%$  (or greater) increase in revenues (procyclical)  
- Why?: proportional taxes (VAT), social transfers, progressive taxes.
- Expenditure Elasticity = 0 or less
- Most of expenditures don't depend on output (for example: public sector wages)  
- Unemployment insurance is a countercyclical component.

# DERIVATION OF CYCLICALLY ADJUSTED FISCAL BALANCE

# INTERPRETATION

Boom:

$$
Y > Y ^ {P} \rightarrow T ^ {C A}, G \leq G ^ {C A} \Rightarrow
$$

The cyclically adjusted balance is less than the general balance (countercyclical)

Recession:

$$
Y <   Y ^ {P} \rightarrow T ^ {C A}, G \geq G ^ {C A} \Rightarrow
$$

The cyclically adjusted balance is greater than the general balance (countercyclical)

CYCLICALLY ADJUSTED BALANCE RULE  

<table><tr><td></td><td>Normal</td><td>Boom</td><td>Recession</td></tr><tr><td>REVENUES</td><td>100</td><td>105</td><td>95</td></tr><tr><td>CYCLICAL REVENUES</td><td>0</td><td>5</td><td>-5</td></tr><tr><td>Adjusted REVENUES</td><td>100</td><td>100</td><td>100</td></tr><tr><td>EXPENDITURES</td><td>105</td><td>110</td><td>100</td></tr><tr><td>BALANCE</td><td>-5</td><td>-5</td><td>-5</td></tr><tr><td>CYCLOCALLY ADJUSTED BALANCE</td><td>-5</td><td>-10</td><td>0</td></tr></table>

- Structural budget rules: consider other items, commodity prices.  
- Over-the-cycle balance rules: require an attainment of a given nominal budget balance ceiling on average over the cycle.

# Chile's Formula to Calculate Structural Fiscal Balance.

The structural balance indicator can be expressed as:

$$
\begin{array}{l} B E _ {t} = B e _ {t} - T N M I N _ {t} + \left\lfloor T N M I N _ {t} \left(\frac {Y _ {t} ^ {*}}{Y e _ {t}}\right) ^ {\gamma} \right\rfloor - T M I N _ {t} + T M I N E _ {t} - I C C _ {t} \\ + I C C E _ {t} - I C M _ {t} + I C M E _ {t} \\ \end{array}
$$

where:

$BE_{t}$  = structural balance in period t

$B e_{t}$  = effective balance (accrued) in period t

TNMIN  $t =$  net non-mining tax revenue and social security in-payments in period t

TNMIN\*t = structural net non-mining tax revenue and social security in-payments in period t

$TMIN_{t}$  = income from taxation of private mining companies in period t

$TMINE_{t} =$  structural income from taxation of private mining companies in period t

$Y e_{t}$  = effective GDP in period t  
$Y^{*}_{t}$  = trend GDP in period t  
$ICC_{t}$  = effective transfers from CODELCO on account of copper sales in period t  
$ICE_{t}$  = structural transfers from CODELCO on account of copper sales in period t  
$ICM_{t}$  = effective transfers from CODELCO on account of molybdenum sales in period t  
$ICME_{t}$  = structural transfers from CODELCO on account of molybdenum sales in period t  
$\varepsilon$ $=$  GDP elasticity of tax revenue

"Set limits on total, primary or current spending, and the limits apply to nominal or real expenditure"

- Positive: easy to understand, monitor and enforce.  
- Negative: when set as percentage of GDP, they are procyclical.

# EXPENDITURE RULES

# Geographical Distribution of expenditure rules in the EU

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/2d885fb5321c0ac2f4da6f1733777cda4fee927b28ff4b81e22d6e1c92b502a6.jpg)  
Note: National rules include those covering the general government (GG) and central government (CG).

# The expenditure benchmark

This benchmark is a rule which contains the net growth rate of government spending at or below a country's medium-term potential economic growth rate, depending on the country's position in relation to its medium-term budgetary objectives (MTOs).

Under the expenditure benchmark, spending increases which go beyond a country's medium-term potential economic growth rate must be matched by additional discretionary revenue measures.

The expenditure benchmark complements the medium-term budgetary objectives (MTO) by putting growth in net expenditure on a sustainable path and therefore helping to move towards or maintain the MTO itself.

The expenditure benchmark was introduced as part of the 2011 reforms (the so-called "six pack").

EU expenditure benchmark targets an aggregate of expenditure which excludes the following items: interest spending, expenditure on EU programs fully matched by EU funds revenue and cyclical elements of unemployment benefit expenditure. In addition, investment spending is averaged over a four-year period to smooth the impact of any large investment projects.

![](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2025-12-02/e320e3ce-bce3-4ea4-b81b-eb889a99b911/fb710259706ca2f99c720fbd614cf838ab60cd31352e85a45af17871108f6b80.jpg)

- Positive: may boost revenues or prevent excessive tax burden.  
- Negative: may complicate macroeconomic stabilization.

# At first sight, the use of fiscal rules is, on average, correlated with stronger fiscal positions…but

Legal Strength: political commitment (1); coalition agreement (2); statutory (3); international treaty (4); constitutional (5). Independent Monitoring and Enforcement Body: No (0); Yes (1). Flexibility to Respond to Shocks: No (0); Yes (1). Correction Mechanisms and Sanctions: No (0); Yes (1). The sum of the scores for each feature included in the fiscal rule is then scaled by 10.
